Two Major Sports Meets in Jiangsu 109

Second Provincial Amateur Sports Meet

Dates: September 18th to 20th

National Games Preliminary

Dates: September 21st to 22nd

Location: Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Public Stadium

Since Jiangsu Province initiated the Amateur Sports Meet in 1929, the country has gradually paid attention to and promoted amateur sports. Recently, the Ministry of Education promulgated the regulations for the Amateur Sports Meet in order to popularize it. Jiangsu Province has been determined to hold a provincial amateur sports meet every year. Last year, due to various reasons, it was unable to continue. This year, it has been decided to hold the Second Provincial Amateur Sports Meet at the Provincial Zhenjiang Public Stadium from September 18th to 20th. The competing units will still follow the precedent of the first meet, dividing the province into eleven districts. The sports events, except for swimming and baseball, will follow the National Games regulations. It is reported that the organizing committee has already sent the regulations and registration forms to various counties and districts.

After the opening of the Amateur Sports Meet, the National Games Preliminary will be held on the 21st and 22nd. In addition to selecting athletes with excellent results from the Amateur Sports Meet, teams and track and field all-around events composed of students from various schools in the province can also register to participate.

Local News

Rice Price Nearing 20 Yuan 118

Price Control Fails, Price Rises Another Yuan Yesterday

High-Quality White Rice Sells for 19.5 Yuan per Stone

The Shanghai Rice and Bean Trade Association previously held a meeting and decided that the highest price for white rice should not exceed 17 yuan per stone, with lower grades priced accordingly. The situation was reported to the Social Affairs Bureau for record. Retail rice shops in Zhabei became panicked and rushed to buy rice. Yesterday, they secretly raised prices in what was called an "unofficial market," with top-grade white rice rising to 19.5 yuan. An investigation revealed that the retail rice shops had previously been wary of stockpiling rice due to the hot and humid weather, fearing insect infestation and grain damage. Now that autumn has arrived, their rice reserves are depleted. Moreover, due to the heavy rains and floods in the interior, the supply of rice has become scarce. In previous years, even when rice prices rose, various types of imported rice were available as substitutes. This year, however, aside from a small amount of Saigon rice and machine-milled rice (also known as Min Dang rice), the rest is domestically produced. Yesterday, no rice arrived at the docks. All the rice boats had arrived in the previous few days, and the boat owners were hoarding their goods, unwilling to sell them cheaply. Under these circumstances, the shops had no choice but to secretly raise prices and compete for rice in order to supply the market. The rice prices from yesterday are listed below, generally showing an increase of about one yuan per stone compared to the previous day. Glutinous rice increased by 1.2 yuan. The details are as follows: Highest grade white rice: 19.5 yuan per stone (the above is the purchase price, the selling price must be 20 yuan, and so on). Next grade: 18.8 yuan. Next grade: 17.5 yuan (i.e., third-grade white rice). Early rice: 17.4 yuan. Pudong new rice: 17 yuan. Bian Yuan glutinous rice: 16.7 yuan (previously sold for 15.5 yuan). Imported Xian rice: 17.5 yuan. Next grade: 17 yuan. Du Xian rice: 17.5 yuan. Next grade: 17 yuan. Ke Xian rice: 15.5 yuan. Next grade: 14.5 yuan (the above are all domestically produced). Machine-milled rice: 16.5 yuan. Saigon rice: 15.4 yuan per 200 pounds (equivalent to one stone, previously sold for 10.02 yuan) (the above are imported rice).

Anti-Japanese Design Association Drafts

Five-Year Plan to Boycott Japanese Goods 119

Li Quanshi, Xu Yongzuo, and Kui Tingfang to Draft Plan

Industrial Fund to be Levied on Raw Materials Approved

Letter to Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to Advise All Industries Not to Use Japanese Seafood

The Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee held a design meeting yesterday and decided to appoint three committee members, Li Quanshi, to draft a five-year industrial plan as a comprehensive backup plan for a complete economic severance with Japan. At the same time, it also passed important proposals such as levying an industrial fund on essential industrial raw materials and establishing a yarn factory for the dyeing and weaving industry. Furthermore, the Anti-Japanese Association has continued to seize Japanese goods in Nanshi, Zhabei, Huxi, Pudong, and other areas in recent days. Details are listed below:

Design Committee Meeting The Anti-Japanese Association's Design Committee held its fourth committee meeting yesterday at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce meeting room. The attending committee members included Li Quanshi, Li Wenjie, Zhu Wenqi, Xu Yongzuo, Chen Songyuan, Que An , Feng Yixian, Zhou Jingshen, Ma Shaoquan, Kui Tingfang, and fifteen others. Li Wenjie was elected as chairman, and Xue Guangqian as recorder. Matters reported: (1) A total of 31 opinion letters were received, summarized into 21 categories and included in the discussion items. (2) Xue Guangqian was appointed as the secretary of the association, and Hu Jingan as the clerk. Next, matters resolved: (1) The executive committee submitted that the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Dyeing and Weaving Industry Federation had initiated an automatic fundraising campaign to establish a yarn factory, which was approved and filed for record. (2) For essential industrial raw materials, all industries should voluntarily organize raw material factories and levy an industrial fund within two months. Before the factories are established, the association will review requests from the industry associations and temporarily issue passes for those that are indeed essential industrial raw materials, provided that the fund is levied and held in trust. This fund will be transferred when the industry establishes its factory. (3) The association has received many letters from the public offering opinions, and should publish acknowledgements in the newspaper. (4) In the future, when factories need to continue to determine essential raw materials, they should apply through the trade associations or national goods groups to prevent abuses. (5) The association should send telegrams to party departments and chambers of commerce across the country to promptly organize anti-Japanese and overseas Chinese aid associations. The above five proposals were all passed and recommended for adoption and implementation by the executive committee. (6) The proposal to formulate a five-year industrial plan as a comprehensive plan for a complete economic severance with Japan was passed. Li Quanshi, Xu Yongzuo, and Kui Tingfang were appointed to draft the plan. (7) The proposal to elect standing committee members of the association was approved. Li Wenjie, Zhu Wenqi, and Lu Qisheng were elected as standing committee members. (8) The proposal to temporarily hold meetings once a week due to the busy work of the association was approved.

Do Not Use Japanese Seafood The Design Association suggested sending a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to advise all industries not to use Japanese seafood. The letter stated: "We are writing to inform you that seafood is largely imported from Japan. According to customs records, the annual import volume is alarming, with tens of millions of dollars in profits flowing out. We use our hard-earned money to allow the Japanese to manufacture weapons to kill our compatriots. Thinking of this is heartbreaking. Just imagine that the Japanese arbitrary violence in Korea, even if it is not delicacies, must be bloody. If you recall the corpses of the dead overseas Chinese compatriots all over the field, even if it is as beautiful as jade food delicacies, it is difficult to swallow. Our Association is entrusted by people from all walks of life to uphold the ambition of lying down and trying courage, and vigorously implement economic severance with Japan, and vow to make the final struggle. Since Japanese seafood is not a necessity of daily use, it can be refused without using it. Donating the subtle sweetness of the teeth and cheeks to save the madness of the collapse, its benefit to the anti-Japanese movement is not fresh and rare. Correspondingly, please check and transfer it to the relevant industry associations, and follow it together. I am deeply looking forward to it. "

Soliciting Opinions from All Sectors The Anti-Japanese Association issued a notice yesterday stating: "Since the establishment of the association, we have received many valuable opinions from people from all walks of life, which can be used as a guide. We are deeply grateful. Some people have also visited the association to give advice, which is even more heartwarming, patriotic and enthusiastic. In the future, if there are any opinions on anti-Japanese aid to overseas Chinese and reforms to the association's measures, please send them to us to benefit the association and promote the anti-Japanese movement."

Continued Seizure of Japanese Goods in Various Places The association's inspection department released the 8th, 9th, and 10th seizure reports as follows: (1) 8th report, August 3rd, 20 boxes of soap at the North Railway Station, August 4th, 32 pieces of purple copper wire from Yongli Company, 32 boxes of Changshi cloth from the Maigen Road vessel, 3 pieces of bicycle parts and 1 piece of sandpaper from the Yongxing Bicycle Company at the Huache Station, August 6th, 3 small boxes of glass from the Sentai Hing Glass Company at the 16th Pier, 4 reams of paper from Datong, 3 reams of paper from Zhang Xintai, 28 small packages of synthetic thread, 11 boxes of glass from Maoxin at the South Railway Station, 52 boxes of large and small glass from Shenda, 1 bag of fish skin from Dada Guangfeng at the Dada Wharf, another bag of fish skin from Dada, 2 pieces of lead skin, 6 coal shovels from Shenda, 8 boxes of glass from Sen Gongtai at the 16th Pier, 5 pieces of hemp bags from Xintai, 1 piece of blue cloth from Longmao at Pudong, 2 wooden boxes of umbrellas from the Da Ma Tou in Puxi. (2) 8th report, August 7th, 600 lattice bottles from Xieshang, 250 small bottles of Xingren, 100 Changbai bottles from Xibaoxing Road, 10 bags of white sugar sold by Shihe Foreign Firm to Baodaxiang on Baoshan Road, 1 bundle of white pine dominoes from Yangsongji on Zhaojia Road, 25 small packages of yarn from Huang Yufeng, 30 packages of printed clothing from Hua Ji at the South Railway Station, 2 pieces of large and small machine parts from Fuxing Ren, 14 packages of printed clothing from Xie Yuanji. Navigation News After the Typhoon Passed 123

The wind in this city weakened slightly yesterday. The Jianghai Customs believed that the typhoon had passed and that there was no danger on the sea, so it ordered the Pudong flag station to lower the warning ball and allow ships to leave the port. It was found that the typhoon had not had a major impact on this city. The information is summarized as follows:

Imports Greatly Reduced Yesterday, all the Jianghai ships that were sheltering from the wind on the way were unable to sail. At the same time, there were typhoons in Fuzhou and Qingdao, so only four foreign ships and one sea ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday. Even the Yangtze River ships did not arrive in Shanghai.

Ningbo Ships Arrived The Shanghai-Ningbo ships were suspended due to the typhoon the day before yesterday. As the wind gradually subsided yesterday, there were no ships coming from Shanghai-Ningbo, so there were no exports. However, yesterday afternoon, the China Merchants Sanbei Company received a telegram from Ningbo stating that the Xinjiang, Tianning, and Xinglun ships had decided to leave Ningbo for Shanghai and are expected to arrive today. The Shanghai-Ningbo ships will operate as usual today.

Nanhua Ship Sailed Yesterday afternoon, the wind weakened slightly. The Swire Company's North and South Ocean ships, Xinjiang and Fengtian, sailed in the afternoon, first to Wusong. If the sea was calm, they would go directly to export. In case the waves were still huge, they would moor in Song and wait to export today. Therefore, a total of twenty-four ships sailed out of the Huangpu River yesterday.

Xujiahui

Change of Director of the Observatory 124

Meier He Hosts a Farewell Banquet

Father Laoh, Director of the Xujiahui Observatory, has now retired and will be succeeded by Father Qi. Mr. Meier He, the Chief Commissioner of Customs, hosted a banquet for the two fathers at his residence last night (11th). Minister of Finance Song Ziwen and Director of Customs Zhang Fuyun did not attend due to business. Others present included French Consul General Gan Ge Lin, Customs Commissioner Laufut, Customs Patrol Supervisor Hill Meng, Howard, editor of the North China Daily News, Zhang Zhuping, manager of the Shen Bao, Dong Xian Guang, manager of the Continental Daily, and He Bo Si Ge Lin. Chief Commissioner of Customs Meier He delivered a speech, roughly saying that the cooperation between the Xujiahui Observatory and the Customs has been going on for more than a day, so the retirement of Father Lao this time is a matter of special attention in the Customs. Former Chief Commissioner of Customs Hede established meteorological stations in various customs in 1869, which was the beginning of scientific research. He intended that the area covered by each meteorological station along the river and sea should not be less than 20 degrees of latitude and 10 degrees of longitude, so that valuable meteorological reports could be recorded. As for the cost, in addition to the purchase of instruments, little was given. At that time, the Chinese Customs' observation of meteorological stations was of great value to the scientific community, and it was especially beneficial to the navigation community in the Eastern seas. This is generally recognized. Over the years, the Xujiahui Observatory began to observe meteorological periods and collect valuable statistics. In 1879, a typhoon passed through Shanghai, and its momentum was very strong. The Xujiahui Observatory accurately predicted the direction of the typhoon. Customs Patrol Supervisor Peishi Pi, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and various shipping companies contacted the Xujiahui Observatory and requested it to establish a meteorological station and issue forecasts on a regular basis, so that the public could be aware of the movement of typhoons in Chinese waters. Later, under the guidance of the fathers, it gradually developed. In 1896, Father Lao became the director of the Meteorological Department of the Xujiahui Observatory. Except for two sick leaves in the middle, he held an important position for a long time until last year. Since the death of Father Yalgui, Director of the Manila Observatory, Father Lao is the most famous typhoon expert in the world.

Meier He Hosts a Banquet for the New and Old Directors of the Observatory, with Father Lao Sitting in the Middle and Father Qi on the Left 125

Page 14

He has contributed a lot to the shipping industry in the Far East and human society, which is worthy of admiration. Father Lao is a world-renowned scientist and mathematician, who has used his life's experience and knowledge to serve mankind and fulfill his obligations purely and without any reward. This is something that we deeply admire. Because Father Lao's forecasts on storms are reported at any time, many ships have been preserved, so the shipping industry must be deeply grateful to him and bless him together. I am very honored to take this opportunity today to praise the father's achievements and thank him for his warm assistance. We are very sorry for the father's departure, but we are also happy for the gain of the successor. The new father will be able to fulfill the duties of Father Lao and maintain the reputation of the Catholic Church with great satisfaction and excellent results. We can foresee. On the one hand, we hope that Father Lao will have unlimited happiness in the future, and on the other hand, we wish the new father success and are willing to continue to cooperate with the Observatory, not only as an obligation, but also as a right to be enjoyed. Then, Father Lao delivered a reply, roughly saying that he was very ashamed and grateful for the praise from Chief Commissioner of Customs Meier He. His only achievement was to be in office for a long time and to do his best to implement the plans of the two previous fathers, Dan and Xue, and to follow the rules. Over the past 50 years, he has received a lot of support from the Customs. Now, on behalf of myself and the Observatory, I would like to thank Chief Commissioner of Customs Meier He and the Customs. If our station did not receive the support of the Customs, the two concession authorities, the Chamber of Commerce, the Telegraph Bureau, and the shipping company, it would not have been possible to achieve such results. Former Chief Commissioner of Customs Hede, various Customs Commissioners, and various Patrol Supervisors have all generously helped and had a very harmonious relationship with our station. The reason why China can have a complete meteorological station and satisfactory results is that we must thank them for establishing storm reporting stations along the coast and transmitting signals to various places. From Niuzhuang to Shantou, all rely on their strength, and the gradual improvement of the signals will be adopted by various countries in the world, and they have also contributed a lot. I have been in office for many years, and once I leave, I cannot help but be moved. However, there is no need to worry about the successor. The new father has helped at our station for 12 years, which is enough to prove his ability. He is deeply convinced of the importance of this position, and is the same as me, and during my vacation, his management is also very satisfactory. In the future, he will be able to continue to maintain the achievements of the past, so the new father's succession to this position is worthy of celebration. I am very grateful for the welcome from Chief Commissioner of Customs Meier He, and I would like to thank you on his behalf.

French Concession Taxpayer Meeting

Inauguration of Supervisory Committee Members Yesterday 126

Resolved to Request Reduction of Housing Tax by One Percent

Should Increase Chinese Directors and Reorganize Merchant Corps

The French Concession Taxpayers' Association of Chinese held its second inaugural meeting of the Supervisory Committee yesterday at 4:00 PM. Committee members Jin Liren, Gong Jingyan, Dong Kechang, Shang Mujing, Wei Tingrong, Zhu Shengmao, Cheng Zhusun, Tong Lizhang, Shen Zhongjun, Xie Qianggong, Li Huailiang, Xu Xiuting, Qu Zhenhua, Bei Zairong, Chen Dezhang, Lu Bohong, Tao Leqin, Pan Zhaobang, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng (representing Shang Mujing), Xu Caicheng, Huang Jinrong (representing Gong Jingyan), Yuan Ludeng, Lou Hongjun, and 24 others were present. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Inauguration of Committee Members After all the committee members entered the room and took their seats, the entire group stood up and saluted the party's national flag. The committee members then bowed to each other and were officially inaugurated.

Meeting Proceedings The meeting was presided over by Cheng Zhusun and Shang Mujing, with Tong Lizhang as recorder. First, Cheng Zhusun reported on the past negotiations with the French Municipal Council regarding the increase of Chinese directors and committee members. He stated that previously there were only three Chinese directors, appointed by the French Consul-General. After the association raised its request, the number was increased to five, and nine Chinese committee members were added, all formally elected by the association. However, among the nine committee members, only three were able to participate in the meetings of various groups, while six remained unassigned, which was as good as a formality. Therefore, the association must continue to actively negotiate. Regarding the association's financial issues, after the charity fair held in 1927, there was a surplus of over 17,000 yuan. After continuous expenditures, there was still a remaining balance of over 3,000 yuan. A detailed report is being printed and will be distributed soon for verification. In addition, all proposals will be discussed separately. Next, Shang Muqin reported on (1) a letter from Chairman Du Yuesheng, requesting to resign from his position as chairman because a Chinese director could also serve as chairman of the association; (2) that future association affairs should be handled by the chairman on a daily rotating basis; (3) that he hoped that all committee members would conscientiously take responsibility for their duties to facilitate progress. Next, committee members Yuan Ludeng, Xie Qianggong, Tao Leqin, and Qu Zhenhua expressed their opinions, which were all incorporated into the proposals for discussion.

Resolutions (1) On the resignation of Chairman Du, it was resolved to retain him, and Qu Zhenhua, Zhu Shengmao, Xu Xiuting, Li Weiliang, Tao Leqin, Ye Weizhai, and seven others were nominated as representatives. (2) Regarding the proposal to reduce the housing tax, it was resolved to reduce the tax from the previously stipulated 1.4% to 1.3%. Given the current prosperity of the market and the increase in housing construction, the Municipal Council's revenue has also increased. The previously retained one percent of the tax should be promptly implemented and reduced, with collection still at 1.2%. (3) Regarding the proposal to improve the tax collection method, it was resolved that in the future, if the rent is in silver, the tax should be collected based on the silver amount to ensure fairness. (4) Regarding the continued request to increase the number of Chinese directors, it was resolved to increase the number of Chinese directors based on the proportion of Chinese and foreign taxes to ensure equality, and to negotiate with the French Municipal Council after consulting with the Chinese directors first. (5) Regarding the request to reorganize the merchant corps, since the cessation of the Sino-French Volunteer Corps, the association has repeatedly requested the French authorities to reorganize the merchant corps. The French authorities had agreed to the organization, but it has not yet been realized. The association should continue to urge its implementation. (6) Regarding the proposal to prioritize the employment of Chinese in the French Concession public service, it was resolved that since the Public Concession's practice of prioritizing the employment of Chinese in its offices had yielded good results, the association should write to the French authorities to follow suit. (7) Regarding a citizen's inquiry about whether the French Municipal Council's new purchase of land in the western district was necessary, it was resolved to report after a detailed investigation.

The Wei Sheng Steamer Ran Aground Off Xiamen 128

The Ship Is Unlikely to Be Salvaged

All Passengers Rescued

The Comprador Fell into the Sea and Died

Due to the hurricane at sea, all coastal steamers of various companies in Shanghai were suspended. The Wei Sheng, a Southern China steamer of the British Jardine Matheson & Co., was sailing from Hong Kong to Shanghai. Due to the storm, it ran aground off Xiamen, causing damage to the ship, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, a reporter investigated the matter and learned that the ship had taken on water and the passengers had been rescued. They may arrive in Shanghai today. The follow-up report is as follows:

Circumstances of the Accident The Wei Sheng was carrying cargo and passengers from the ports of Hong Kong and Guangdong to Shanghai. On the morning of the 10th, when the ship arrived at Nanwan (transliteration) off Xiamen, it encountered a hurricane at sea. For safety reasons, the captain, Mr. Hoxhis, decided to seek shelter in the Nanwan Strait. Unexpectedly, the waves were large and the water was turbulent, causing the bottom of the ship to strike a reef. The reef punctured four large holes in the bottom of the ship, and seawater rushed into the ship, causing it to sink, creating a very dangerous situation.

Rescue Efforts When the ship had the accident, the captain tried to send a direct telegram, but it could not get through. He first sent it to Jilong, and then Jilong relayed the telegram to the Shanghai and Hong Kong offices, requesting them to send ships to help rescue. The Shanghai office received the report and immediately telegraphed Jilong, asking them to send a ship nearby to rescue. After the Hong Kong headquarters received the news, it ordered the Heng Sheng, which was in Hong Kong, to sail to Nanwan to rescue.

Passengers Rescued When the Heng Sheng arrived at Nanwan, the main cabin of the Wei Sheng was already flooded and was about to sink. Because it was difficult to tow it out of the shallows at that time, the Heng Sheng had to lower lifeboats into the sea to rescue all the passengers and crew members of the Wei Sheng and then sailed to Shanghai. It may arrive in Shanghai today.

Comprador Fell into the Sea During the Wei Sheng accident, the wind and waves at sea were extremely strong. A comprador on the ship happened to come out of the cabin and was on the deck when a large wave hit him. The comprador was swept into the sea, and his body has not been found. Although the crew members of the ship tried to search for him, they have not been able to find him.

Ship Damage The Wei Sheng is an excellent ocean liner in the Jardine Matheson Southern China fleet, with a load of nearly 3,000 tons. This time, it carried a large amount of cargo and passengers from Hong Kong, Guangdong, and Shantou to Shanghai. According to the telegram from the company yesterday, the total loss of the ship, cargo, and private goods is at least around one million.

Pinghan Railway Traffic Resumes 129

However, Two Transfers Are Required

The China Travel Service received a telegram from the Beijing-Shanghai Railway stating that traffic on the Pinghan Railway has fully resumed since the 5th. However, two transfers are required: one at Guangshui Donghuangdian for reloading and one between Hankou and Jiaji for ferrying. However, first and second-class tickets south of Xinyang cannot be sold until the railway notifies them.

Customs

Detention of Naval Material Incident 130

The Inspector General of Customs's Talk

On the 8th of this month, a report stated that the Jianghai Customs refused to allow the Naval Ministry's aircraft factory to retrieve aircraft engine and other parts shipped from England, causing dissatisfaction among the Naval Ministry authorities with the Jianghai Customs. A reporter from this newspaper met with Mr. Frederick Maze, the Inspector General of Customs, yesterday and talked about the matter. According to Mr. Maze, the Customs has always complied with the special regulations promulgated by the National Government regarding the reporting of military equipment, aircraft, and other national goods. For those that require tax exemption, it is necessary to request approval from the Ministry of Finance, which will then instruct the Customs to verify and exempt the tax. Only then can the Customs release the goods tax-free. The Customs itself has no right to exempt or detain any goods without reason. Although the aircraft parts, etc., reported by the Naval Ministry's aircraft factory held a passport approved by the National Government for import, the Customs had not received an order from the Ministry of Finance to exempt the tax. The factory had also not submitted a tax exemption passport from the Ministry of Finance for verification. Therefore, the Customs was unable to allow the tax-free retrieval of the goods. Therefore, the Customs had no intention of deliberately creating difficulties in this matter.

The disaster is especially severe in Pengshui, Xiushan, and Kai County in eastern Sichuan, Guyi, Junlian, and Hejiang in southern Sichuan, Yingshan in northern Sichuan, Quancheng, and the Beijiang River basin in central Sichuan. Thousands of families have been destroyed, and hundreds of thousands of people are wandering without food or shelter. With the jackals in the province running rampant, it is difficult to call on help. Listening to the refugees crying, our hearts are torn apart. The conference has always been concerned about hunger and drowning, and our Sichuan is happy to rely on benevolence and kindness. We hope that the righteous grains will be delivered early so that the disaster victims can be saved. If we can get flesh and bones, we can raise all beings from hell. We will definitely embroider with colored silk and burn incense on Mount Emei. We earnestly appeal and ask you to give alms. We hereby send this telegram and beg you to understand. The Sichuan Fellow Countrymen's Association bowed in truth.

Social Bureau

Yesterday's Summons of the Printing Industry for Questioning 136

Three Days of Shutdown, Wages to Be Paid Temporarily

Treatment Conditions to Be Agreed Upon by the Industry

After the resumption of work in the printing industry in this city, the Social Bureau summoned them yesterday for questioning in order to mediate the treatment conditions. Representatives from the Ming Printing Industry Association, Zhang Yixin and Chen Bingxi, and representatives from the Printing Industry Union, Qu Shoukan and Wang Yaoquan, attended. The meeting was presided over by Zhang Shuye of the Social Bureau, and recorded by Wang Zhiqin. The labor side demanded that wages be paid for the three days of shutdown and that methods be found to mediate the treatment conditions as soon as possible. The capital side stated that the shutdown was caused by the workers' automatic change to 80 hours and refused to pay wages. As for the conditions, they must be discussed with the entire industry before negotiations can take place. After repeated guidance from the chairman, it was decided that the capital side would temporarily pay wages for the three days of shutdown. Regarding the treatment conditions, the capital side was required to consult with the entire industry and respond within one week. After the response, a mediation committee will be convened to formally mediate.

There Is Still Local News on the Following Page 143

Page 15

Local News

Five Children Seek Immortality and Leave 144

Harm Caused by Divine, Strange, Martial Arts Novels

Planned to Go to Mount Emei

Ran Away the Night Before, Destination Unknown

Shop Owner Anxious, the Departed Nowhere to Be Found

Last spring, in March, five boys in Shanghai, each just over ten years old, saw through the vanity of the world and together set off for Mount Emei to study Daoism. This became a popular anecdote for a time. Fortunately, one of the boys was young and timid, unaccustomed to hardship, and deeply homesick, crying constantly. Eventually, his elder brother sent him home. Meanwhile, the families of the other boys were also searching for their whereabouts everywhere. Upon seeing this young boy return, the other four were also eventually found. Their grand ambition to cultivate Daoism thus remained unfulfilled. Do these boys perhaps still regret their past actions? It is unexpected that such things happen more than once in the world. Recently, five more boys in this city, infatuated with the heretical martial arts tales of sword swallowing, pill spitting, and cloud soaring, formed a group to seek immortals and enter the mountains to study Daoism. These five boys were all apprentices, with insufficient clothing and no travel expenses. Before setting off, they pawned their clothes to raise money. Most amusingly, on the day of their departure, each of the boys burned incense and lit candles, swearing to the gods that anyone who showed cowardice or regret would be punished by heaven. Such actions reveal the depth of their poisoning by divine and strange heresies. These boys ran away the night before last and have not been heard from since. They left behind no possessions for their shop owner to remember them by, except for twenty-odd small volumes of "The Burning of the Red Lotus Temple" in comic book form, found in a broken sack. These martial arts books, with both pictures and text, are likely the starting point for the boys' pursuit of the Dao. Education authorities should pay close attention to such semi-divine, semi-fantastical popular reading materials.

Five Apprentices with Similar Interests, a Group of Five to Study Daoism and Seek Immortality: All were apprentices aged around seventeen or eighteen. The leader, Chen Hexiang, was nineteen years old and an apprentice at a foreign goods store. The others, in order, were Wang Lianfu, nineteen years old; Zhang Ciguan, nineteen years old; Zhang Yaokui, eighteen years old; and Yao Sheng, seventeen years old. Except for Zhang Yaokui, all were from Ningbo. Wang Lianfu and Zhang Ciguan were apprentices at Yang Yunxing's sofa workshop, located at No. 153, Lane 8, De'an Lane, North Shanxi Road. Zhang Yaokui was an apprentice at Yang Rongxing's furniture store at No. 179 Beijing Road. Yao Sheng was an apprentice at Yun Shengtai's sofa workshop. Thus, these five were similar in age and background, and their thoughts easily converged. Chen Hexiang was likely the most literate among them, so his thirst for knowledge was more acute. He was the one who instilled the heretical ideas of studying Daoism.

A Lodger in a Pavilion Led the Disciples: Chen Hexiang previously worked at Bao Xing Foreign Goods Store on Xiamen Road. Recently, seeking better prospects, he lodged with his friend Yu Heming. Yu worked with straw hats and lived in Yang Yunxing's pavilion. Therefore, he was able to associate frequently with his Daoist companions Lianfu, Ciguan, Yaokui, and Yaosheng. The stores of Yang Yunxing, Yang Rongxing, and Yun Shengtai were all opened by Yang Yunsheng. Thus, these five apprentices had many opportunities to meet and talk. Moreover, it was the height of summer, and late-night gatherings to escape the heat provided ample opportunity to discuss divine and strange matters. Thus, this strange play of seeking the Dao gradually matured. Chen Hexiang, the lodger in the pavilion, had little knowledge but was impressed by the talk of gods and Daoism. He loved reading divine and strange novels such as sword immortals and martial arts stories, including "Investiture of the Gods," "Journey to the West," "Seven Swords Thirteen Knights," and "The Marvelous Adventures of Jianghu," which he knew by heart. He was fascinated by the magic of alchemy and swordplay, so his words and expressions were always tinged with the supernatural. When he saw Wang Lianfu and Zhang Ciguan, he confusedly spoke of the Dao and used divine and strange tales to lure them. Thus, within half a month, the two apprentices Wang and Zhang were led by Chen Hexiang and baptized by the heretical teachings of martial arts and the supernatural. The second step was their contagion of Zhang Yaokui and Yaosheng. From then on, the five children shared the same path, all immersed in the cauldron of the supernatural.

Daoist Children Embark on Their Journey in Peculiar Attire: In the past half month, the five's attitude changed drastically. Their actions became secretive, and they often discussed matters privately, as if deliberating on important events. Among the five, Wang Lianfu was the eldest, followed by Chen Hexiang. Wang and Chen were particularly close, so the two were revered as leaders within this small group and called "Elder Brother" and "Second Brother," meaning elder sworn brothers. In addition to indulging in Daoist beliefs, Chen, the "Elder Brother," also worried about national affairs. He was greatly indignant about the Wanzai Massacre and often muttered, clenched his fists, and stretched his legs, vowing to save the country with divine immortal martial arts. The children, already immersed in novels like "The Burning of the Red Lotus Temple," readily agreed and eagerly sought the Dao in Sichuan. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 1 p.m., they gathered at the entrance to swear an oath to the gods. At that time, an apprentice happened to pass by and overheard them saying, "Anyone unwilling to depart shall be struck by lightning and burned by fire." At 6 p.m. that evening, this group of Daoist children seeking immortality gathered at the entrance of De'an Lane and departed. According to eyewitnesses, the attire of each child was peculiar and worth amusement. The eldest brother, Wang Lianfu, wore a white twill short shirt and pants, with a black mole on his face for identification. The second sworn brother, Chen Xianghe, wore a undershirt and shorts, holding an oiled paper fan with a solemn Daoist appearance. The third brother, Zhang Ciguan, wore a blue cloth short shirt and pants as Daoist clothing, with one foot in a torn satin shoe and the other in a torn cloth shoe, reportedly due to a hasty departure. The fourth brother, Zhang Yaokui, was dressed similarly, wearing torn white canvas sneakers, speaking with a Jiangbei accent, which was his distinctive feature. Yaosheng, the youngest, had large, double-lidded eyes and brought up the rear, wearing a foreign gauze shirt and pants. The five gentlemen disappeared into the setting sun, never to return.

Shop Owners Anxious, Searching Everywhere: After the five children left, the shop owners were baffled, believing they had run away, and were indescribably anxious, searching everywhere for their whereabouts. It is said that these five apprentices seeking the Dao had repeatedly said they wanted to go to Mount Emei in Sichuan to seek immortals and cultivate Daoism, and they outlined their plan as follows: departing from Shanghai, walking to the South Railway Station, taking a train to Hangzhou, and staying there to cultivate immortality if there were famous monks or heroes. Otherwise, they would resolutely enter Sichuan to seek immortals on Mount Emei. The shop owners initially thought it was a joke and did not take it to heart. Who knew it would actually happen? After the five children left, their companions searched for their belongings but found nothing. All clothing that could be pawned had been pawned to pay for travel expenses. All that remained were dozens of divine and strange books, which caused the shop owners great heartache.

Ye Zengshou Kidnapping Case

Ye Must Appear in Court 145

Without His Presence, the Case Cannot Be Clarified

Judge Instructs Ye's Wife to Inform Him

Two Men from Mazhuang Have Been Released

Ye Zengshou, owner of the Zhongfu Import and Export Company at No. 17 The Bund, was kidnapped on the morning of the 4th of last month, at 10:30 a.m., while accompanied by his third concubine, Mrs. Ye, as they were leaving their residence at No. 369 Yulin Road in his private car, license number 4529, intending to visit a doctor on North Sichuan Road for his eye ailment. Just as he boarded the car, he was abducted by kidnappers who sent a letter demanding a large ransom. Ye has since been released, and the Hua detective Wang Xichang of the Bund Police Station has arrested two kidnappers, Xu A'gen and Chen Xingjiang. The Public Security Bureau has also detained two accomplices, Ma Deda and Zhuang Zhangsheng, who have been sent to the police station and transferred to the First District Court for interrogation. These details were reported in this newspaper yesterday morning. Judge Feng Shide presided over the continued trial in the Second Criminal Court. Ye Zengshou did not appear, but his wife, Mrs. Ye Fu, appeared with her legal representative, Lawyer E'sen. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the police station presented the case, stating that Xu A'gen and Chen Xingjiang were being prosecuted under Articles 1 and 2 of the Regulations for Punishing Kidnappers. On July 20th, at 9:45 a.m., detectives from the Bund Police Station arrested the defendants Xu A'gen and Xu Rongfu at No. 160 North Shanxi Road. Xu Rongfu has since been released. Chen Xingjiang was subsequently arrested at No. 32 Xiangyin Road, Jiangwan. The other two, Ma and Zhuang, were detained by the Public Security Bureau. Xu and Chen were involved in the kidnapping of Ye Zengshou. After kidnapping Ye, they took him to Zhangjiajiao in Jiangwan and hid him in Chen Xingjiang's house, with Xu A'gen and Chen Xingjiang responsible for guarding him. After ten days, Ye was released for a ransom of ten thousand yuan. Xu stated at the police station that he received one hundred yuan, and Chen received thirty yuan. The police station has been unable to find any connection between Ma Deda and Zhuang Zhangsheng and the kidnapping case. The house in Jiangwan belonged to them, and they rented it to Chen Xingjiang, so the police station is not prosecuting Ma and Zhuang and requests their release. Mrs. Ye Fu stated that after her husband, Ye Zengshou, was kidnapped on the 4th, she received a letter from the Water Police Department on the 14th, stating that Ye had been released. She then went to Hangzhou to meet him. Ye is currently recuperating in Putuo and dares not return to Shanghai, so he is not present today. Judge Feng stated that Ye must appear in person to clarify the case and instructed Mrs. Ye to have her husband surrender himself next time. Otherwise, a subpoena would be issued, and if he refused to comply, he would be arrested. The chauffeur, Mei Guigen, testified that on the morning in question, he was driving to the intersection of Yulin Road and Sheng Road when three robbers suddenly appeared, brandishing guns. Two were in front, and one was in the back, ordering him to be silent. When the car reached Baoding Road, the robbers forced him and the third concubine out of the car. He then reported the incident to the first concubine, who reported it to the police station. Xu A'gen testified that he did not go with them when Ye Zengshou was kidnapped. Afterwards, someone asked him to go and guard the hostage at Chen's place in Jiangwan. The hostage was in Room 26, and there were four guards. After about ten days, he heard that Ye had been released for a ransom of ten thousand yuan, negotiated by a man named Uncle. Afterwards, he went to the Zhongnan Restaurant in Dapuqiao in the French Concession, where Uncle gave him one hundred yuan. Chen Xingjiang testified that on July 3rd, an Uncle came to his place and wanted to rent a house for a few days, which would be returned soon. He then rented Room 26 next door. The next day, three people entered and stayed for eight or nine days before leaving. Later, Uncle gave him twenty yuan. Judge Feng verified the testimonies and ordered Xu and Chen to be detained for another fourteen days for further interrogation. Ma Deda and Zhuang Zhangsheng were investigated by the police station and found to have no criminal suspicion and were granted release.

Granddaughter of the Late Sheng Sues for Inheritance

Sheng Aichen's Estate 146

Sues Mao Zengnian, Sheng Yuyou, et al.

Requests the Return of the Embezzled Inheritance

Sheng Rong, 35 years old and married to a Wang, granddaughter of the late Qing Dynasty Grand Guardian Sheng Xingsun, recently hired three lawyers—Xu Bingcheng, Chen Tingrui, and Li Zuyu—at the First District Court to sue Mao Zengnian, Sheng Yuyou, Sheng Enyi, and others for jointly embezzling her inheritance, along with related civil claims. The court has approved the summons and scheduled the trial for the 15th of this month. The plaintiff's complaint is recorded below:

Regarding the defendants' joint embezzlement of the inheritance, the plaintiff requests the court to impose criminal penalties according to the law and to make incidental civil claims. The plaintiff was born to Sheng Kuichen, the eldest son, and adopted as a daughter by her third uncle, Sheng Aichen. In 1919, Sheng Aichen passed away from illness, leaving no children. At that time, only Sheng Aichen's concubine, Madam Gong, the plaintiff's stepmother, and the plaintiff were present at his bedside. The plaintiff personally witnessed the encoffining and performed all the rites expected of a filial child, including wearing mourning clothes, carrying the staff, buying water, and embracing the body into the coffin. The defendant Sheng Yuyou was the son of the defendant Sheng Enyi, who was residing in Beijing at the time. Later, the grandmother, Madam Zhuang, chose Yuyou to be Sheng Aichen's son. At that time, he was still young and did not come to Shanghai for the funeral. Later, Yuyou came to Shanghai with his birth mother but never lived with Madam Gong. The plaintiff then married Wang Jiuli. On the afternoon of May 18th of this year, when Madam Gong passed away, the plaintiff and her husband happened to be in Hangzhou. Upon hearing the news, they rushed back, wore mourning clothes according to custom, and in her grief, did not attend to the inheritance. All the funeral rites for Madam Gong, including the seven-day rituals, the funeral procession, and the temporary placement of the coffin, were overseen by the plaintiff. According to custom, the son-in-law's family must organize the fifth seven-day ritual, which the plaintiff also did. For the sixth seven-day ritual and the funeral procession, the plaintiff and her husband led their children to escort the coffin to the Yongshan Hall in Suzhou. On August 2nd, after the completion of the funeral, they returned to Shanghai and learned that the newspapers had published a notice that Sheng Yuyou had sued the defendant Mao Zengnian (Madam Gong's cousin) for theft, but the case was dismissed. After further investigation, the plaintiff learned that the defendants Sheng Enyi and Yuyou, along with his birth mother, had taken advantage of the chaos of the funeral to secretly withdraw Madam Gong's valuable jewelry from the safe deposit box in the Siming Bank. Furthermore, the clothes, gold, and silverware left behind were also sealed off, intending to embezzle the plaintiff's share of the inheritance. Therefore, Mao Zengnian wanted to take advantage of the situation and hid six passbooks from Madam Gong's accounts at the Siming Bank, the Shanghai Bank's Kadlu Road branch, and the Wuzhen account, totaling one hundred thousand yuan, along with a seal. Yuyou and his birth parents urged him to hand them over, which led Sheng Yuyou to sue Mao Zengnian for theft. However, they did not dare to proceed with a public trial, and Yuyou withdrew the lawsuit. The collusion between them is evident. Both parties originally intended to harm the plaintiff's right to inheritance and embezzle her share. First, they quarreled over the uneven distribution of the spoils, and then they secretly divided the spoils and settled the lawsuit. Such ghostly behavior is a joint act of embezzlement, violating Article 356 of the Criminal Code. In addition to reserving the right to sue Sheng Yuyou's birth mother, the plaintiff urgently requests the court to approve the summons of the defendants for questioning, impose criminal penalties according to the law, and, based on the incidental civil claims, order the defendants to hand over all of Madam Gong's embezzled inheritance, so that the plaintiff may receive her rightful share according to the law, to uphold justice and protect her rights.

Public Utilities Bureau

Rectifying Privately Run Ferries 149

Limiting All Ferries to Rebuild New Ferries and Docks

Adding City-Run Ferries Until Compliance

The privately run ferry between Qichangzhan on Pudong and Weisaigong Pier on Puxi has been taken over by the Public Utilities Bureau since the 10th of this month. Previously, on July 29th, the Public Utilities Bureau received a phone call from the River Police of the Jianghai Customs, stating that "The ferries prepared by the Zhenxing Company between Qichangzhan on Pudong and Weisaigong Pier on Puxi are narrow and old. Every day, from 6 to 7 a.m. and 5 to 6 p.m., thousands of workers cross the river, resulting in several drowning deaths. Today, a small ferry used for towing was loaded with several times the number of passengers allowed by the customs license. The port police of the Customs enforced the ban, ordering a portion of the workers to go ashore first in order to load them in batches to avoid repeating the past mistakes, which led to verbal conflicts and fights. The situation with the ferries of the Fuxing Company is similar. However, if we revoke the licenses and order them to stop running, traffic will be disrupted, and workers will not be able to cross the river. If we allow them to continue operating, the ferries will be in violation of regulations every day, with unthinkable consequences. Managing the ferries is the responsibility of the municipal government. Could your ferries take over the service to maintain transportation?" The bureau immediately sent staff to conduct an on-site inspection with the River Police of the Jianghai Customs, recognizing that the ferry crossing was important and in need of urgent remediation. In order to protect travelers and maintain transportation, the bureau decided to operate the ferries while ordering the companies to build new-style ferries and proper docks within a reasonable period of time, and only after the inspection is passed would they be allowed to resume operations. The bureau then reported to the municipal government for approval on August 1st, which was approved on August 4th. Preparations were immediately started, the Qichangzhan pier on Pudong was slightly renovated, and the city ferries No. 6 and No. 7 were transferred to begin service on August 20th. All related agencies are requested to assist. On August 8th, the Fuxing and Zhenxing companies were ordered to build formal docks and new-style ferries according to the city's ferry regulations within eight months of receiving the notice, otherwise, the service would be taken over by the city. Furthermore, since only one company is allowed to operate each ferry crossing, they were ordered to merge into one company through negotiation. It is also reported that the city-run ferry will still charge each passenger four copper coins, and the service will run from 4:45 a.m. to 7:30 p.m. daily.

Representatives of Shipping Companies

Requesting a Wider Definition of Wharf Shoreline 150

Representatives of shipping companies from Puxi, including Xing Zhigang, yesterday jointly submitted a petition to the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau and the Land Bureau, requesting a wider definition of the wharf shoreline and asking the municipal government to register the case in order to build docks and benefit transportation. Various businesses along the Punan area have mainly relied on inland shipping for trade with the countryside. The Wanyu, Gongyi, Dongjiadu, and Jinan Guild Hall wharves have historically been used by ships from the five counties of Puxi, Songjiang, Fengxian, Shanghai, Nanhui, and Chuansha. During the seventh year of Xianfeng in the Qing Dynasty, the Shanghai merchants Deyi, Daheng, Wanxiang, Senmao, Hecheng, and Wanyu petitioned the Shanghai County Magistrate Huang regarding the berthing of ships, requesting the erection of stone tablets at the wharves to allow berthing in perpetuity. The tablets still exist today, with clear inscriptions that can be easily verified. The petitioners are now concerned that the wharf shoreline is gradually being occupied by the ferry bureau. They previously petitioned the Port Authority, which replied that the bureau was currently planning a comprehensive public wharf in the Punan area to ensure that merchants would not face any problems with existing wharves. The ships berthed at the area between Jinan Guild Hall and the Wanyu wharf are all over forty meters long, with an average of fifty to sixty ships arriving daily (a list of shipowners is attached). The wharves are narrow, and latecomers must line up far into the river, unable to dock, and passengers and goods cannot be unloaded. Ships from neighboring towns arrive and depart with the tide, and they do not stay overnight. Those who fear missing the tide carry their goods on their backs, risking their lives to walk on the uneven wooden rafts, and are prone to falling, a hardship that those who have not experienced it cannot imagine. This is because the defined shoreline is narrow, causing this danger. The petitioners believe that wharves and roads are equally important. The Jinan Guild Hall and other wharves are well-known wharves in Punan and the commercial center of the area. Thousands of people rely on them every day, and tens of thousands of dollars worth of goods are transported daily. Furthermore, the annual ship tax revenue is considerable. The bureau is in charge of the shoreline along the river and should define the measurement of the wharves to maintain transportation and benefit traffic. Therefore, the petitioners jointly petition your office, hoping that you will review and approve the petition, send staff to remeasure and define the shoreline of the Wanyu, Gongyi, Dongjiadu, and Jinan Guild Hall wharves, and register the case with the municipal government to build docks and prevent others from encroaching on the land. This would not only benefit the people of the five counties in Puxi but also the future of Punan's commerce. The petitioners eagerly await your decision.

Methods for Strictly Suppressing Bandits and Kidnappers 151

Advising Citizens to Assist

The Police Department of the Shanghai French Concession Municipal Council, in order to curb crime, is offering rewards for information and advising residents to assist in the investigation and arrest of criminals, for the benefit of detection. A proclamation is hereby issued stating that when Chinese residents within the concession encounter extortion, threats, robbery, and other such incidents, they often offer considerable resistance. As a result, such cases have gradually decreased. However, lurking bandits are still a potential threat in the long term, and optimism is not warranted. Such criminals are timid as mice and only use intimidation to prevent victims from resisting, allowing them to act as they please. If victims were to resolutely offer courageous resistance, they would be powerless. Currently, the concession has over five thousand well-trained and armed detectives who are either spread out on the roads or stationed in police stations. Once a warning is received, they can be dispatched immediately. When the public is in danger, they only need to sound a whistle to call the police or go to a nearby police station to report the incident. This is a beneficial and cost-free option, so why not take advantage of it? The detectives are public servants of the people, supported by public funds, and serve society. They only need opportunities to engage in investigation and arrest, and they will naturally be enthusiastic and committed to their duties. Members of high society who are aware of suspicious or criminal individuals in their vicinity can report directly to the police station or submit a written report. The heads of the police stations will keep these reports strictly confidential and make every effort to investigate. For confidential matters, individuals can report directly to the head of the Criminal Division at his office or by mail to Room 331, No. 331 Henan Road, Municipal Council. Robbers and kidnappers are organized into gangs and hold optimistic views. Their first step is to instill fear in the public. Those who carry out the acts are often instructed by others, and those who instigate the crimes are familiar with social conditions. This is almost always the case in kidnapping cases. Therefore, wealthy families must be cautious about hiring servants and partners and making friends. If someone is unfortunately kidnapped and someone comes forward to negotiate the ransom, the family must pay special attention to the person and consult with friends who have had similar experiences. It may be possible to discover that these people are accomplices from previous incidents. Kidnappers are well aware of the fearful psychology of the hostage and do not hesitate to repeatedly exploit their relatives and friends. Although criminal gangs may temporarily evade the law by taking risks and seeking fortune, they will inevitably be caught one day. Therefore, they are more worried about their schemes being exposed than the victims. If the victims can provide information to the police station, these criminals will not be able to escape the law. Those who carry out the kidnapping are merely puppets who are blinded by small gains and forget the greater harm. They are not worthy of attention. After the criminals are caught, the victims should be bold and testify in court to provide evidence so that they can be severely punished according to the law. If anyone conceals the details of the kidnapping, they will only embolden the criminals and even bring harm to their relatives and friends. The leaders of the criminal gangs often pretend to be members of high society, indulging in extravagant spending on wine, women, gambling dens, and brothels, using ill-gotten gains to squander. When their money runs out, they have no choice but to find a suitable person among their friends to sacrifice and seek ways to recoup their losses. Regarding the ransom, if the police station is consulted in good faith in advance and cooperates fully, using money as bait to lure the criminals into capture, it cannot be considered illegal. However, most victimized families do not understand the situation and are unwilling to truthfully report the ransom negotiations to the police station, even fabricating lies in an attempt to escape guilt. This is tantamount to aiding the evildoers, leading to the misfortune of their relatives and friends, and must be considered illegal. Any landlord who directly rents a house to a criminal gang, or indirectly through a sub-landlord, is also in violation of the law, as their intention is to make money and they lack a sense of public good. Landlords and sub-landlords have a responsibility to society to cooperate with the police station to reduce crime and ensure local peace. Otherwise, even the best police station in the world will not be able to fully function without the adequate assistance of the public. The Chinese often encourage their children with the saying, "Everyone should sweep the snow from their own doorstep and not worry about the frost on other people's roofs." Therefore, most Chinese are unwilling to interfere in the affairs of others. However, for the sake of public peace and tranquility, all residents of the concession have a shared responsibility to maintain local law and order. Although the concession has repeatedly cracked down on major thefts and punished the perpetrators according to the law, there have recently been occasional cases of armed robbery. This is due to the public's lack of a spirit of mutual assistance. The methods for assisting the police station can be divided into the following three points: (1) Robbers usually enter through the front and back doors due to the negligence of servants. It is best not to let strangers or suspicious individuals enter after dark. (2) Few victimized families sound the alarm or call for help. It is difficult to report to the police in the presence of robbers or because they are unable to do so. However, once an alarm is sounded, the robbers will flee in terror. This shows that robbers are not brave people, and they dare to act as they do because the residents are cowardly and allow them to rob and plunder. If the victimized family does not make a sound, the detectives will have no way of knowing that a robbery has occurred and will have no opportunity to catch the robbers. Therefore, if residents are unfortunately robbed, they should immediately sound the whistle, ring the gong, call for help, etc., to attract the attention of neighbors and detectives so that they can come to their aid. (3) If a neighbor encounters a robbery, they should sound the alarm, call the police by telephone, or follow the robbers and wait for an opportunity to report to the police and arrest them in the spirit of mutual assistance. Residents of the concession, in order to reduce theft and assist the police station, should not leave windows open, leave clothes on the drying rack, or leave bicycles unattended on the side of the road. Furthermore, do not allow criminals and suspicious individuals to loiter in playgrounds, markets, public trams, automobiles, and parking lots, as they often mingle in these places to steal items from pedestrians' pockets or grab women's jewelry and purses. If such incidents occur on the road, it is advisable to report them to the police as soon as possible. There is also a type of social pest that often appears at train stations, hotels, teahouses, theaters, and gambling dens, specializing in deceiving the ignorant and soliciting gamblers for gambling dens. These people first use enticements, and those who fall into their trap will lose all their assets. These pests are not only found in this city but also in major cities around the world. As long as these people are not imprisoned, new disasters will emerge endlessly, and countless people will be harmed. The public must pay close attention to the above-mentioned issues and provide assistance in a timely manner to gradually eliminate the bandits in the area so that merchants and residents can live and work in peace. This is of utmost importance. The Police Department has sufficient rewards available. In the future, anyone who comes forward with reliable and confidential information, regardless of age or gender, will be given appropriate rewards to encourage them once the information is verified. This proclamation is hereby issued. July 29, 1931, Police Chief Mao Ding.

American Sailor Burell Dies from Bullet Wound to the Head 152

Suspected Suicide

The Ta Mei Evening News reports that American Marine Corps serviceman Burell died from a bullet wound to the head in his barracks on Xinzha Road at 6:45 PM yesterday (the 10th). Suicide is suspected. This morning (the 11th), American officials conducted an autopsy and investigation. Burell was only 25 years old. Friends said that he appeared to be in good spirits five minutes before his death and showed no signs of depression. The reason for his suicide is unknown.

Zhang Chongren to Study in Europe 153

To Study Art and Newspaper Business

Mr. Zhang Chongren, a diligent young scholar with expertise in art, is highly regarded among Western-style painters in Shanghai. He is a distinguished student of F. Enri. He is skilled in painting, especially photoengraving. He is the first person in the Far East to create photoengraved zinc plates. After several years of study, Mr. Zhang has lived up to his teacher's expectations. He is honest and unpretentious and studies tirelessly. He served as the editor of the Tushu Shibao for four years with remarkable achievements. In his spare time, he devoted himself to painting and created many masterpieces. Recently, he was selected by the Gengkuan Committee to study fine arts in Europe, as well as to investigate the Western newspaper industry and economic conditions. It is reported that Mr. Zhang is scheduled to leave the country on the 18th of this month. His relatives and friends will hold a farewell party at Moore Memorial Church at 4:00 PM on the 15th.

(6) The water gate and masonry workers have completed one and a half years of work, but the company considers them short-term workers, so there is no Sunday work. Now they demand to be treated the same as long-term workers. Resolved: To be handled by the board of directors and supervisors. (7) Gu Taoxiu is not a foreman and has arbitrarily added new workers. How should this be handled? Resolved: The union will send a letter ordering the withdrawal of the new workers. (8) Xu Rongsheng, Lao Guansheng, and Tang Gensheng, deceased members of the carpentry department, should the company fill their vacancies? Resolved: Passed. (9) How should the unreasonable oppression of workers by Westerners in the factory be handled? Resolved: If oppression occurs, first notify the comprador. If the Westerners do not change their ways, then a response will be considered. (10) The company's comprador requested the union to allow the company's engine room to add short-term workers to the drainage vehicles. Resolved: The company is permitted to add short-term workers to the drainage vehicles, and a notice will be issued. The meeting adjourned.

Military Uniform Industry Union: Yesterday, the 8th board meeting was held, chaired by Sun Xin. Discussion Matters: (1) A letter from the representative of the contractors stated that the price list for contracted goods had been agreed upon by all contractors through unified measures, requesting assistance in notifying all contractors to ensure uniform compliance. Resolved: To comply. (2) Factories are about to resume work. How should non-union workers be handled when they work in the factory? Resolved: (A) A letter will be sent to the contractor representative to fulfill the agreement. (B) The union will advise non-union workers to complete their membership. (C) If there is a situation of borrowing union cards to take someone's place, how should it be handled? Resolved: If the above situation occurs, the union card can be revoked. (D) The wages for Zhongshan suits and cycling pants made of Emerald Lawn cloth have not increased, but the contractors have instead reduced them. How should this be dealt with? Resolved: (A) For work that is the same as before, wages should be increased by 10%. (B) If the work is more complicated, wages should be increased by 20%. (C) Yu Zhixun and Sun Xin will be appointed to negotiate with the contractor representatives.

Acknowledgement: We received a complimentary copy of the Bank Weekly, issue number 711, from the Bank Weekly yesterday. Thank you.

Weather Report 165

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 pm yesterday stated that the coastal area here is mostly cloudy, there is a strong southeasterly wind in the East China Sea, the Yellow Sea has a gentle wind with no fixed direction, the Shandong coastal area is overcast and rainy, and the middle reaches of the Yangtze River also have rain due to the receding hurricane. Another hurricane in the Pacific Ocean is approaching Gan, moving in a north-northwesterly direction. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 pm yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 91.9 degrees, and the lowest was 80.1 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 95.2 degrees, and the lowest was 76.1 degrees.
