Free Talk

A Word or Two 167

— Yi Mei

Famous gardens often have scabby walls. Famous flowers are easily broken.

Opening the south window in summer, splashing ink to create freehand flowers and plants, is incomparably pleasant.

The prescriptions of quack doctors are no different from the death warrants of demons.

Struggling under the oppression of life knows neither cold nor heat.

Women, regardless of beauty or ugliness, all consider adornment as their second life.

In civilized lands, those who die unnaturally must be more numerous than in uncivilized villages.

A flower or a blade of grass in front of the courtyard has its own charm. There is no need for thousands of acres of gardens. A book in the room has its own ancient charm. There is no need for ten thousand scrolls on the shelf.

One's heart should not be blinded by wealth. One's will should not be disturbed by wine.

When writing letters for others, even if you exert your full strength, only nine-tenths of your talent will be seen.

Those whose footprints do not reach dance halls and swimming pools are definitely not modern figures.

People in Wu call the leader of thugs "red old man". In fact, the term "red old man" was used in the capital during the Song Dynasty to insult soldiers. It can be seen that proverbs must have origins, but repeated transmission and misinterpretation inevitably leads to loss of original meaning.

The principles of the world are cyclical. Therefore, what is new becomes old after a long time, and what is old becomes new again.

The sunlight is to be feared, so it is covered with curtains. Therefore, curtains are the staunch defenders against the sun.

Striving is the spirit of ambition. Humility is the virtue of scholars.

Reading in winter and summer, touring in spring and autumn: this is the only blessed person in the world.

Emptying the wastepaper basket brings great comfort to the heart.

The ancients banned opium to show concern for worthy people. Today's ban on opium achieves the effect of rejecting poison.

Illness can be cured, so one should seek treatment when sick. Poverty is incurable, so worrying about poverty is not as good as accepting it.

A Record of the Capital's Orphans' School 168

— Jie Fei

This summer, I attended the Lishi Society's summer school and rented a place at the National Revolutionary Army Orphans' School outside Zhongshan Gate. The school is located on the southern hill of Sifang City, at the foot of Zijin Mountain. The Zhongshan Mausoleum stands majestically to the left of the school. With the wind, rain, morning, and dusk, one can embrace the mountain scenery to the east and admire the sacred monuments to the north, and cannot help but think of the high mountain and great conduct. Therefore, I record its outline to mark my fleeting visit.

A Glimpse of the Architecture: The school was prepared in November of the 17th year of the Republic of China and opened in March of the following year. In December of the 19th year, the boys' and girls' schools were separated. The girls' school moved to Yangpi Lane in the city. The new buildings for the boys' school have been completed, with a total of 36 large and small buildings. They cost 250,000 yuan. All are old-style bungalows, with the Zhongshan Hall located in the center. The remaining buildings form a constellation-like surrounding. Zhixin Courtyard, Boxian Courtyard, and Keqiang Courtyard are the most prominent.

Student Life: Most of the school's students are admitted successively. To date, there are more than 400 students. Their native places span 17 provinces, from Suiyuan in the north to Guangdong in the south. Among them, those from Hunan province are the most numerous, accounting for about one-third. Jiang, Zhejiang, Anhui, and other provinces are next. The oldest is 20 years old, and the youngest is 5 years old. The older ones wash their own clothes. All expenses are免收免收. Moreover, most of the school provides the study and living supplies. The first issue is quilts, bedding, clothes, and utensils such as boxes and bowls. The subsequent issues include shoes, socks, soap, tooth powder, toothbrushes, and towels, which are issued monthly by the dormitory affairs department. A monthly allowance of three yuan is also given, but most of it is deposited in the bank. Gifts from relatives are limited to fruits, clothes, and stationery. There are no holidays. Students stay in school all year round except for special circumstances. This is because their fathers and brothers were national martyrs, and their families rarely have possessions.

Love, Sincerity, and Integrity: The school takes "Love, Sincerity, and Integrity" as its motto, which is divided into eight major goals: making life laborized, making behavior disciplined, making spirit egalitarian, making physique martial, making thought scientific, making interest artistic, making organization socialized, and making the school familial. After living there for a long time, I realized that the people there were quite capable of striving to practice it.

Rural Center: The principal of the school is Mr. Chiang Kai-shek. The director of education is Mr. Shi Xiangzai, an advocate of rural education who acts on what he says. He intends to use the school as a rural center to promote outward. Therefore, the school's junior high school only offers agricultural courses. There is a farm of 500 acres. Students cultivate most of the vegetables themselves. The fields are lush and green. They harvest in the morning and evening for their meals. This is just an extra activity.

Famous People's Couplets: There are many couplets by famous people in the party and country hanging in Zhongshan Hall. Mr. Hu Hanmin's couplet says: "Comforting the descendants of benevolent martyrs, no virtue can repay their sacrifice; advancing children and teenagers in learning, aspirations will surely be fulfilled." Mr. Dai Chuanxian's couplet says: "Do not forget that your virtuous fathers and brothers took righteousness and achieved benevolence. You must study hard today. You must learn to be a great man and establish yourself in the world. You must strive to defend your country in the future." Mr. He Yingqin's couplet says: "Having thousands of mansions, happily sitting together in the spring breeze, happily nurturing talents for the country's use; may our comrades not waste their time, but cultivate virtue and follow the example of their predecessors." The kind and benevolent words are indeed inspiring and make people feel endlessly admired.

Fresh Scenery: The school is located within the mausoleum area, so the main roads are fully opened, new houses are planted everywhere, and pines and cypresses sing, wisteria and vines shade the scenery, flowers fill the fields, and fragrant grass fills the valleys. This makes people feel as if they are in a vast swamp and forest. When the sun rises above the eastern mountain and the moon shines between the evening cities, facing the mausoleum to the north and welcoming the warm breeze from the south, taking two or three young students from the school, and talking about the events of their fathers and brothers riding horses to kill thieves, one cannot help but feel a sense of sorrow and excitement in one's heart.

The Strange Pagoda on Tianma Mountain 169

— Ying Dai

There is also a strange pagoda on Tianma Mountain in Songjiang. It is nine stories high. To this day, only the core of the pagoda remains. It is impossible to climb the mountain. One can tell at a glance that it is an ancient pagoda of a thousand years. What is even stranger is that the lowest two stories of the pagoda have extremely large cracks. The entire pagoda is tilted at a 15-degree angle. However, for the past ten years, it has not fallen. Next to it is a ginkgo tree, with a trunk that can be embraced several times. It is an old tree. The branches of this tree all curve towards the pagoda. Even the tender branches and leaves all face north towards the pagoda. As a result, ordinary ignorant villagers all say that this tree is magical, and that the pagoda has not fallen because of the support of the tree. This pagoda and this tree are indeed strange objects. Therefore, I record them.

A Record of Recent News from Gan River 170

— Sun Choucheng

Yesterday, I met Mr. Tan Yanhui, a disaster relief commissioner of the Party and Political Affairs Committee of the Commander-in-Chief of the Land, Sea, and Air Forces' Headquarters, at the Red Cross. Mr. Tan had just come from Gan. The situation he described is worth recording. I think it is also what those who care about the current situation would like to hear.

Separate Governance: There are a total of eighty-one counties in Gan Province. Forty-three counties have been ravaged by the Communist bandits. After Commander-in-Chief Chiang personally went to suppress the Communists, he organized the Party and Political Affairs Committee of the Commander-in-Chief of the Land, Sea, and Air Forces' Headquarters. Those with established reputations serve as committee members. Counties occupied by bandits are not subject to the control of the Jiangxi Provincial Government after their recovery, but are governed by the committee. Therefore, at present, only thirty-eight counties in the entire Jiangxi Province are under the jurisdiction of the Provincial Government. Forty-four counties are under the command of the committee (because one of the original forty-three counties was vast and has been divided into two counties). Separate governance has achieved remarkable results.

Flying Every Three Days: Commander-in-Chief Chiang went to Gan this time with the determination to "have me without bandits, or have bandits without me." Every time he instructed officials, he used these two sentences to encourage them to advance and fight. Because a certain regimental commander was timid and did not advance, he was severely punished to warn the various divisions. As a result, the military's morale was firm and they moved forward bravely. Therefore, they were invincible wherever they went. Although Commander-in-Chief Chiang was stationed in Nanchang, he was fully aware of the situation on the front lines. Every three days, he would take a red airplane to the front to personally inspect the battle lines and give instructions in person. The various military officers were therefore very inspired. Everyone said that the airplane's comings and goings were quite eye-catching. It was the height of summer. The Chairman should take a break. Commander-in-Chief Chiang said that as a general, he should share the joys and sorrows with the soldiers and do his best for the country. It was the duty of a soldier, so he continued to fly every three days as usual.

Ten Thousand Needles Piercing the Heart: The tragic death of Zhang Huizan, the former commander of the 18th Division, has been seen in various newspapers. Recently, a small bandit who had personally witnessed Commander Zhang's death was captured among the Communist bandits. What he said contained details that were not known to outsiders. According to him, after Commander Zhang was captured, the bandits tried to persuade him to surrender, but he refused. They then pierced his nostrils with iron rings, dragged him through the streets, and ordered his trusted officers to whip him with leather whips. They lured him with great profits. Zhang still refused. When asked what his purpose was, he said that he only wanted to meet the Commander-in-Chief. Even if he died, he would have no regrets. The bandits laughed and said that it could be done. They then ordered the small bandit to buy more than a dozen packages of sewing needles and a bowl of cold water, and forced Zhang to swallow them. Zhang said that since he could not meet the Commander-in-Chief in life, he hoped that his remains would be sent to him after his death. Then he would die in peace. The bandits agreed to his request. They then forced him to swallow the needles. After a while, his face turned white, and he rolled around on the ground, pointing at his heart. The scene was too horrible to look at. The so-called ten thousand arrows piercing the heart in old novels was nothing more than this. The bandits watched him die, then cut off his head, placed it on a board, and put it in the river to float downstream. They laughed and pointed at Zhang's head, saying that he could now go and see his Commander-in-Chief. Their cruelty was like this.

Travel Notes on India (78) 171

— Ling Hua

After arriving in India on the 8th, I had contact and observations with people from all walks of life in India, and my thinking changed. First, from the requirements of Indian culture and people, I learned that in the future, the national cultures of all Asian nations will be combined into a large federation. Then, connecting with the Americas to form the Pacific East Asian Federation. This is only a matter of time to decide to evolve this situation. The British scholar Wei Ershi had already said it, and he also said that world unification must be in the hands of nations that speak Chinese and English. He can be called a wise man. I had this idea many years ago. Now, I must decide to implement it because of the requirements of the Indian people. Second, observing Gandhi's movement and the life of the Indian people, I learned that transforming society, especially in Chinese society, India's spiritual life and the spiritual power of the spiritual movement are very suitable and easy for Chinese people to adopt. Because cultural elements have similar points. India is a large tree, and Buddhism is one of its branches. East Asia has been bathed in Buddhist culture for decades. Spiritual life is very important. It is not comparable to the Russian people. Third, contacting Muslims, I learned that the great power in southwestern Asia lies in Islam. From Shaanxi and Gansu in the east to Europe in the west, one must not underestimate religion. Without knowing its habits and psychology, there is no way to connect. In general, religious issues are no longer a cliché in Europe and the United States. It has become a setting sun. Even in Asia, the relationship between Islam and India is 60% to 70% religious. Conflicts arise because of different hobbies. Marx's theory is definitely not enough to solve it. For example, Indians call cows and conflict with Muslims. There is no economic relationship. It is purely a difference in habits and ideas. Please put Lenin in India. You cannot force Indians to eat beef. It is unchangeable until death. Indians will never become emperors if they eat beef. This shows that habits and beliefs can change life. Life does not depend entirely on matter. Both Islam and Christianity have things that can be adopted. The Japanese Mushanokoji New Village has Buddhists and Christians, which can be proven.

The novice monk told me that Russia's victory was due to its geography. China's geography is not as good as Russia's. It is easily invaded by imperialism. Then, if China does not adopt the Russian system and wants to unite all of Asia, it must compare and study India in the central part, Islamization in the southwest, and Buddhism in East Asia, Japan, Siam, Burma, etc., and synthesize a large federation. It stands between the three major federations of the European Federation, the American Federation, and Russia. I have gained something from Indianization. I want to go to Turchai to study the cultural customs of Islamic and other religions. I will definitely gain a lot. I haven't been able to go yet. But if you live in an Indian place and study Islamization, Indians don't like it. Even if you read their books, Indians will not express sympathy. The difference in national psychology is so great.

Rotary Club Novel

Women, Women (17) 172

— Yao Suifeng

Nothing happened overnight. The next morning, the clerk followed the landlady's instructions, got up early, and rushed to the Railway Hotel, guarding the door, just waiting for Xiao Rong to come out so he could call him back.

At half past nine, he indeed saw Xiao Rong walking out of it with that beautiful woman, looking proud. The clerk hid aside, and when he walked out the door, he unexpectedly walked in front of him and said loudly, "The landlady invites you to come!"

When Xiao Rong saw it was the clerk, he was very unhappy, but he was embarrassed to explode because of Miss Ding. He acted lightly and said, "I know! I'll come back myself in a while. You go first!" As he spoke, he walked forward without even turning his head.

The clerk originally didn't want to let him go, but then he thought that since Xiao Rong said he would come back himself in a while, he would let it go. He went back to report, watching Xiao Rong walking away with that woman, laughing.

Miss Ding asked, "Who was that who called you just now?"

Xiao Rong made a contemptuous expression and said, "Who else could it be? There are too many poor relatives and friends of ours in Suzhou. When they hear that I'm coming from Shanghai, they just want to borrow money from me!" After saying that, he gave a cold laugh. Miss Ding also believed him.

Xiao Rong thought that it would be better to go back in a while to avoid them coming to pester him again. He also thought that he had to move to a different hotel to avoid them finding him again. So he said to Miss Ding, "After we go to Tiger Hill to play, we have to move to a different hotel when we come back, otherwise my poor relatives and friends will inevitably come to borrow money from me again!"

Miss Ding also thought it was a good idea.

Really, after playing at Tiger Hill, they moved out of the Railway Hotel and stayed at the Dongwu Hotel. He also told the tea boy at the Railway Hotel that he had returned to Shanghai.

After moving hotels, he planned to go home. He only told Miss Ding that he was "going to visit a relative's house who had invited him just now, and he would be back in about half an hour."

So, he actually returned to his home with an angry expression. When he walked inside, he saw his father and mother sitting there silently. When they saw Xiao Rong coming back, his father immediately stood up.

"Xiao Rong! You're having a good time! Don't you even think about what kind of person you are?" He slapped the table and said angrily.

Xiao Rong didn't say anything, and actually gave a cold laugh.

"You tell me! Who is that woman? I told you to go to Shanghai to study hard, not to pick up girls! You tell me, who is that woman?" He said, his voice getting louder and louder.

Gold Bar Low Then High 174

Market conditions seem unstable. Yesterday, the 11th, the gold price fell and then rose again, with turbulent waves, advancing and retreating from time to time. There were a total of fifteen taels of fluctuations throughout the day. Industry intentions were vague, and measures were beyond reach. The situation was precarious, resulting in a further rise of four taels. Major players had different demands for supply, but the buying sentiment in the after-market was excited, with bulls increasing their positions and bears rushing to cover. Despite a slight dip in the silver market, it was not taken seriously. Moreover, the European market initially weakened but then strengthened, almost causing gold prices to open lower. While foreign exchange was stable, the afternoon session turned to within 771 taels to outside of 775 taels. The after-market turned from stable to high, likely because exchange rates became increasingly strong. The market suddenly surged, soaring by more than ten taels, exceeding the 80-tael mark again, showing unmatched momentum, but it remains unpredictable.

Morning Opening Reverses to Low. The market opened at 9:00 AM, dropping five taels and one mace to 772.5 taels. Large silver bars contracted by a quarter. Public and private telegrams indicated silver prices were down 3/8 of a cent, but Citibank's buying interest remained strong until after the closing bell. Sellers were very active on the floor, with Wanxing, Shunli, and others initially selling off, causing prices to drop to 771.8 taels. Subsequently, Yuánmàoyǒng, Tóngtàichāng, Yuánchūn, and others bought in. Additionally, initial British gold was at 625, later calculated as 5625, thus rising to 775.4 taels. Afterwards, Yuánxìng, Yǒnghéng, and others came to sell, causing a retreat of three taels. It was also learned that British gold listings would not change, while American gold increased by 125, briefly reaching 772.5 taels, then quickly rising to 774 taels. However, Chāngshēng, Yǒngcuì, Chāngyǒng, and others sold off. It was rumored that speculator Mr. Wu also unloaded, temporarily suppressing the price to 770.07 taels. Despite stable British gold prices, the market reversed and rose again. Fúchāng, Hónglì, Chūnyuán Yǒng, Dàlián groups, Tàichāng, and others agreed to buy, causing a surge of five taels, with some fluctuations of one or two taels up and down. At 10:20 AM, it was at 775.5 taels. Bǐngxìng, Yǒngfēng, Qiánchāngxiáng, and others were active in selling, causing a drop of more than four taels. At 10:30 AM, it was at 771.3 taels, as August and September British gold could settle at 5625. Later, Yǒnghēng, Zhìfēng Yǒng, and others bought in, adding three taels. However, there were no major changes. From 10:00 to 10:30 AM, it was at 4 taels and 4 mace. Afterwards, it was learned that Indian exchange rates were low in the near term but rising in the long term, immediately dropping more than two taels to 772 taels. Subsequently, Yǒnghēng and others bought again, raising it by three taels. At noon, it was at 775 taels. At closing, it returned to 773.5 taels, as the Dàlián group continued to sell, with advertised prices still calculated at 819 taels, a discount of 45-46 taels to over 48 taels. The noon closing was at 45-46 taels.

After-Market Gradually Shows Upward Trend. The after-market opened at 773.4 taels, with fluctuations of one tael and zero mace, but little trading. When Indian exchange rates increased slightly by one anna, the gold price retreated from 773.6 taels to 772 taels. After 2:15 PM, buyers seemed more diligent, raising it by two taels. By 3:30 PM, it was around four taels, with British gold fluctuating around 625. Suddenly, the exchange market tightened, with banks trading among themselves at 5625. Industry players began to scramble, with Yuánxìng, Yǒngfúyú, Chéngfēngyǒng, Zhìfēngyǒng, Yǒnghéngyú dà, and speculator Mr. Luo, among others, aggressively buying. In just half an hour, it soared six or seven taels, exceeding 80 taels by almost 4:00 PM. With British gold settling at only 4375, another five taels were added. By 4:10 PM, it reached 85.5 taels, almost as if it were leaping a thousand feet. However, sellers, such as Qiánchāngxiáng and the Dàlián group, continued to sell, suppressing it again by four and a half taels to 81 taels, then pulling it up again by more than two taels to three and a half taels. At the 4:20 PM closing, it was at 81.6 taels, a continuation of the four-tael increase from the previous day. The maximum price for the day was 85.5 taels, the minimum price was 770.07 taels, a difference of 14.8 taels.

Spot Now Maintaining Its Position. The spot price was 2.3 taels in the morning, 4 taels at noon closing, 4 taels in the afternoon, and 81.5 taels at the closing bell. Advertised prices were discounted by 46-47 taels to 33-34 taels, with the final price at 37 taels. Before bookkeeping, the pre-market was 772 taels to 774 taels, and the after-market was 80 taels to 82 taels. The water top-up was 772 taels in the morning and 80 taels in the afternoon. The spot price of the silver bars only increased by 9.5 mace. Yíngfēnghéng sold several hundred taels of futures to the Dàlián and Tiānjīn groups and bought back three to four hundred taels, sold by various firms from other locations, while the market is holding its position.

Inconsistent Entries and Exits. Furthermore, industry trading on the floor seemed complex. Héngyú, Fúyú, Yǒngfēng, and Chāngshēngyǒng all sold out. Shùnlì, Dàdéchéng, Zhìfēngyǒng, Yuántài, Yuánchūn, Sēnchāngyǒng, Chūnyuányǒng, and Fútàihēng had quite active trading in and out. Cotton Yarn, The Yarn Market Trend Is Still Unstable. 180

The yarn market was stable in the morning and fell in the afternoon. The trend is still unstable. Because the world cotton industry is deteriorating, many people are selling, but most buyers are unwilling to take a heavy loss because the decline is too severe. Therefore, the pre-market is still stable, but there is a lack of buying. There are gradually transactions of crude yarn from the Yunnan group in the current yarn market, but there is a lack of large amounts. In the afternoon, because the price of American cotton was quite cheap and raw cotton was trending down, the bulls closed their positions, and the decline intensified. The future situation is still difficult to determine. The September price has already broken through the 50-tael mark.

The Man-Mark was Stable in the Morning and Fell in the Afternoon. The opening of the Man-Mark pre-market was stable, and the profit-taking parties shorted. The prices for various months rose by 3, 4, and 6 mace. In the afternoon, due to the weakness of raw cotton, the bulls sold off, and the market price fell sharply. The prices for various months fell by 2 taels to 2 taels and 6 mace. At closing, there were more shorts, and the market rebounded slightly. The total transaction volume was 75,850 bales. It was found that Tianlong sold 3,050 bales, Mingde sold 1,250 bales, Rongxing sold 1,500 bales, Shenchang sold 1,000 bales, Yicheng sold 2,100 bales, Xiesheng sold 1,250 bales, Deji sold 1,750 bales, Shenji sold 1,500 bales, and Changfeng sold 2,450 bales. Mingde bought 1,450 bales, Xinchang bought 1,350 bales, Daji bought 1,950 bales, Gengfeng bought 2,500 bales, Yida bought 2,100 bales, Shenda bought 1,450 bales, and Ruida bought 1,550 bales. The Reason for the Continued Weakness of the Cotton Market. 181

Indian Cotton also Shows a Sharp Decline.

Foreign Merchants are Selling American Cotton at Reduced Prices.

The cotton market initially stabilized and then fell, because Indian cotton also showed a sharp decline, and foreign merchants were selling American cotton at special reduced prices in the market. However, the factories have no absorption because they view the world trend as weak and the situation is very pessimistic. Therefore, the cotton market is extremely weak, and the future is still difficult to stabilize. The Japanese merchants are still closing their long positions, and the Flower Mark is bound to see a price of 32 taels.

The Han Mark is Still Weak. The opening of the Han Mark pre-market was due to the disastrous fall in Indian cotton, and the sentiment was not good, but retail investors were short covering. The prices rose by 5 fen to 1.5 qian. In the afternoon, because the price of foreign cotton was extremely cheap, and a large number of open positions were being made, people's hearts suddenly became empty, and the prices fell by 4, 5, and 6 qian. The total transaction volume was 168,600 dan. It was found that Changfeng sold 7,800 dan, Ruiyuan sold 4,400 dan, Yuanchang sold 3,200 dan, Deji sold 3,500 dan, and Tianlong sold 4,500 dan. Grains. New Indica Rice Rises Another Half Yuan. 183

South Market. The sources from various groups amount to about ten or more, but the stock in the river is also scarce. Due to the thin stock in urban and rural stores, coupled with the sharp increase in the price of Xinzha, the desire to buy is increasingly urgent, but it is still not enough for distribution. Therefore, the market atmosphere is tense. As for the market prices of various goods, under the supervision of all sectors, fearing that complications will arise, the association still assesses and opens the prices. Not much Dongxin indica rice has arrived, and the price has increased by half a yuan. Foreign rice arrived today on the 2nd. The go-downs for out-of-town groups and this street are still lively, and the price has increased again.

Xinzha. The sources from various groups amount to ten or more. The rice merchants' association openly assesses and evaluates the prices. Top-quality thick indica rice is scarce, and the go-downs are mostly in the central region. The market prices for top-quality goods are uniformly at 17 yuan. The shape-changed yuan and thin indica rice are still in high demand from tea shops, and the situation has surged by about one yuan. The new indica rice is on par with the South Market.

Mark Flour Changes Several Times 184

Huge Inflow and Outflow Set the Highest Record for Turnover.

Flour Transactions Return to Full-Day Trading Starting Yesterday.

Yesterday in the flour market, after the opening in the morning, the market for each month once again presented a soaring phenomenon. Because the quoted prices of foreign wheat rebounded by 4, 5, 6, and 7 jiao, the people outside the industry were exceptionally excited. The highest price for this month was 2 taels and 1 qian and 9 fen. The deferred months also rose by 2-3 fen. However, after the second session, the market suddenly fell because it was rumored that a large factory had another large order of foreign wheat, rumored to be six or seven ships, with the combined price for bulk cargo being only 4 taels, 2 qian, and 4 fen. Therefore, the factory wharves were dumping, and actual sales were also returning for profit, falling by 2-3 fen from the highest price for the deferred months. Until the afternoon opening, due to the reversal in the morning, people's hearts were not very good at first. Soon, the market rebounded step by step due to short covering and the consistent absorption from the inland areas. Throughout the day, because there were several ups and downs in the market, both buyers and sellers were exceptionally lively. The total transaction volume reached 3.115 million packages, setting a new high record since the establishment of the exchange. As a result, this month rose by 1 fen and 2.5 li compared to the previous day. September and October rose by 2.5 li, November did not move, and December and January each increased by 5 li. The Flour Exchange has resumed full-day trading starting yesterday, with auctions opening at 10:00 AM and 2:30 PM.

Wheat Futures Experience Heavy Selling and Decline in the After-Market 185

Spot Trades Open at 2,100 Packages.

Yesterday in the wheat futures market, after the opening in the morning, the market situation for each month still showed a tense phenomenon. The highest price for this month reached 4 taels, 2 qian, and 3 fen. The deferred months also increased by 3-4 fen. However, afterwards, because of rumors of continued orders for foreign wheat, people's hearts had turned stable. Until the afternoon opening, due to the confirmation of the continued orders for foreign wheat by the factories, and the traders also finalized two ships of bulk cargo, with one ship at 4 taels, 2 qian, and 7 fen and one ship at 4 taels, 3 qian, and 2 fen, the selling became more active. The long positions of a certain major player also smoothly exited while the market was still strong. As a result, they all fell back. It is estimated that this month fell by 5 fen compared to the previous day, September and October fell by 3 fen, November fell by 1 fen, and December fell by 3 fen. The spot wheat market is stable and slightly brisk, with 2,100 packages of wheat from Kaizhitang, Shuangfeng, Hengtang, Danyang, Yangzhou, Gaoyou, and Zhenjiang, etc., being handled by Huafeng Fuxin.

Marine Products Ningbo Dried Baby Octopus New Goods Poor Harvest 186

Small Octopus Sales Sparse, Market Weak

Ningbo Dried Baby Octopus: Old goods have already been sold through. According to reports from Ningbo, this year's new goods harvest is significantly less, not even half of last year's. Therefore, incoming goods are very scarce. A few days ago, mountain traders transported over a thousand catties, selling at 52 to 55 taels. Demand is very brisk, with Zhenjiang and Changzhou merchants buying up all the stock.

Small Octopus: The new goods from various mountains are plentiful. Therefore, the supply is abundant. However, the business of the merchants has not yet taken off, so the inventory in the market is increasing day by day, and the market situation is declining. Currently, peddlers are offering large pieces at 33 taels, high-quality at 27 taels, and ordinary at 26 taels. The market is weak.

Silk and Tea: Large Batch of Improved Autumn Silkworm Eggs Transported to Wuxi 187

Estimated at over one thousand sheets... Product of the Improvement Association

The autumn silkworm season in the interior is about to begin. Zhejiang's Hangzhou and Shaoxing areas are currently selecting eggs to prepare for hatching. Farmers in Jiangsu's Wuxi and other places, who previously ordered improved autumn silkworm eggs from the Shanghai Silkworm Improvement Association, are now receiving the goods in Wuxi. In recent days, the association has transported 1,600 to 1,700 sheets of autumn silkworm egg paper to Wuxi.

Silk and Satin Merchants' Appetite is Weak 188

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign firms' silk market remained sluggish. There has been no improvement in the European and American silk telegrams. Although domestic silk merchants have shown some interest in Shanghai white filature silk, the quantity is limited. Only Wei Cheng and others imported ten bales of Shanghai white filature silk, and Samsung and others imported twelve bales of yellow coarse silk. Prices remained stable.

Foreign Firms' Green Tea Sales Brisk, Prices Rise 189

Yesterday, in the Shanghai foreign firms' tea market, green teas such as Chun Mee, Needle-like, Hyson, and Gunpowder from Wuyuan, Tunxi, Shexian, and other areas were in high demand. Jardine Matheson, Ewo, Tientsin Trading, and other major foreign firms were eagerly searching and buying as much as possible because they received urgent telegrams from overseas and learned that this year's tea crop had been reduced. High-quality Chun Mee from Wuyuan's northern villages has already been offered at 170 to 180 taels. Goods from Tunxi, Shexian, and other areas have also been offered at 110 to 120 taels, an increase of more than ten taels compared to before. For Gong Xi tea, Russian firms and assistance associations are offering 55 to 56 taels. Bai Tou Zhuang and China Tea Company are also continuing to purchase, and the market has risen by four or five taels. The green tea market is showing a trend of stability.

Piece Goods: Observations on the Piece Goods Market after the Boycott 190

Since the boycott of Japanese goods, the piece goods market has been very quiet. Domestic products are in short supply, so any available goods are quickly purchased, making it difficult to find sufficient quantities. Trading in the market remains stagnant. In the Hankou area above Wuhu, anti-Japanese associations have been established, completely halting the sale of Japanese goods. Hankou, having suffered from floods, has seen sluggish demand. Since last week, Sichuan merchants have transported a significant amount of Japanese piece goods, leading to an oversupply. Starting yesterday, there have been fewer buyers. The Tianjin and Shandong merchants have been somewhat active since the stock market crisis ended, transporting over a thousand pieces of satin, moon velvet, and serge. As Yunnan and Guangdong have not yet joined the boycott, there has been some re-export trade. Fine twill domestic goods, which are mainly sold to Guangdong merchants, have been affected by this, causing prices to rise and then fall. Fine cloth is very scarce, while coarse cloth is no longer as firm and expensive as before. Nine-pound cloth is around 5.1 taels, while thirteen-pound Double Horse, Horse Dog, and Double Eagle cloths are around 6.65 taels. Western goods have benefited from previous boycotts of Japanese goods, but this time they have not shown any improvement, mainly due to the extreme shortage of ordinary goods.

Shanghai Market

Market News 210

Fuan Company in Xiaodongmen declares: Our company is the only large department store in the southern city. Our business has always been prosperous. Recently, the original location of our silk and foreign goods department was insufficient, so it has been moved to the second floor and greatly expanded. The various foreign sundries departments have been relocated to the storefront, and new-style glass display counters have been installed. The display of goods is extremely eye-catching. It is said that the arrangement is already in place, and a summer sale will be held soon.

Daxin Silk and Satin Store at the corner of Shilu Sanmalu declares: Our store has always had a fashion department, gathering famous designers to study fashion styles. We pay close attention to women's summer shirts, believing that the current popular styles lack aesthetic concepts. Therefore, we have created a new style that does not require shoulder straps. The price is quite low, selling for only two yuan and eight jiao. Furthermore, our store will hold a one-week anniversary sale in September. At that time, we plan to publish a special issue for circulation. We have now started soliciting essays and designs. Those with excellent works will receive generous gifts to assist with their artistic interests. Detailed rules have been set for this essay solicitation. If you want to request a copy, you can attach a one-cent postage stamp and send it directly to our store.

Guanshengyuan Main Store on Nanjing Road declares: Our company has recently decided to give away 50,000 glass cups within three days, from the 7th to the 9th of this month, to reward customers who purchase fruit dew, in order to enhance their interest in purchasing. The method is that for every large bottle of fruit dew or two bottles of the second size purchased, one cup will be given as a gift for mixing the dew. In the past two days, our main store, the old store in Jiumu, the Henan Road branch, the Fada Malu branch, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce National Goods Market branch, and Guannan in Penglai Market have all been giving away the gifts. It is said that two-thirds of the gifts have already been given away.

Fushou Pharmacy at the intersection of Simalu and Wangping Street declares: The Tu Xue Wan Quan Jiao (All-Around Hemoptysis Cure) sold by our pharmacy has great efficacy and has long been praised by users. This plaster not only effectively treats hemoptysis, but also has special effects on coughing up blood and pulmonary tuberculosis. Satisfaction after use is guaranteed.

Theater News 211

Shanghai Film Company declares: "Eastern Arabian Nights" is the most magnificent production of this year. Yin Mingzhu's portrayal of Princess Amiguo is delicate and charming, unparalleled for a time. The scenery is extremely rich and bizarre, dazzling the eyes. Those who have seen the trial screening praised it unanimously, marveling at it as a rare and outstanding domestic film. It is scheduled to be publicly screened at the Beijing Grand Theater in this city starting August 23rd. At that time, there will surely be a grand occasion.

Calligraphy and Painting News 212

Liangchen Haoyoushe at the intersection of Beijing Road and Zhejiang Road declares: Our society is holding a cooperative fan exhibition of Zhang Zhenlu and Heling Henian. All exhibits are gold fan surfaces. Mr. Zhang Zhenlu created double-line cursive script, and personally recorded five chapters of his novel. Mr. Ma collaborated on meticulous blue-green landscape paintings. Letters are different. Visitors are welcome. The deadline is August 10th. During the period, each piece is sold at a low price of five yuan, which can be added to the inscription. Many pieces have been sold in recent days, and there are not many remaining pieces.

Youth Zone

Feelings 213

— Ge Xiangrong

The weather has been sultry these past few days. Yesterday evening, after I finished bathing, I put on short clothes and pants, slipped on my slippers, and waving a palm-leaf fan, strode out of the house. I took a small bamboo chair and sat down at the back door, enjoying the refreshing breeze.

I had only been sitting for a moment when the sounds of people suddenly became noisy on the steps across the road. I followed the sound with my eyes and saw a rickshaw puller gesticulating and talking to a group of onlookers of various kinds. Standing next to him was a Western woman. As the puller spoke, he shouted at the Western woman in an English-speaking tone, "Money, money!"

At that time, driven by curiosity, and because the matter seemed to have some international flavor, I hurriedly went into the crowd to find out what was happening. It turned out that the Western woman had hired his rickshaw from Route Lafayette in the French Concession and had been pulled all the way to the corner of Jing'an Temple Road and Route Muir Ming, where I lived. She had only given him sixteen copper coins for such a long journey, which seemed too little, so the rickshaw puller was making a fuss, trying to get a few more.

Most of the onlookers thought that such trivial matters were commonplace.

Some called him "mama huhu."

Some said, "It's your own fault. You like to pull foreigners. Usually, when we call their rickshaws, they don't even bother with us. But as soon as a foreigner waves his hand, they get excited, shake their arms, and desperately pull their empty rickshaws to the foreigner, smiling and serving them. This is called a good lesson."

Some expressed slight sympathy, saying, "Sixteen copper coins for pulling such a long way is too cheap."

Everyone was talking at once, expressing different opinions, but no one could come up with a concrete solution.

At this time, the Western woman stood there for a long time, and suddenly rushed out of the crowd. I quickly looked in the direction she was rushing and saw a burly foreign soldier, carrying a small stick, wearing a flattened hat with two short streamers trailing from the back, and a red ball on top of the hat, much like the red button on our melon-skin hats. His military uniform was ordinary, but what he wore below was not right. He had multi-colored pleated pants, with small mirrors and horses attached to them. People who didn't know that this was a special Scottish decoration would definitely find it strange. At that time, the Western woman went up to him and chattered a few words, which I heard were probably words of counter-propaganda. The soldier, without asking anything else, gave the rickshaw puller two small blows, while saying in extremely bad Chinese, "See what thing, go, go." He scattered the crowd of onlookers and led the Western woman away, which I felt was probably their only duty, the so-called "protecting overseas Chinese."

The rickshaw puller, after being startled, saw that the foreign soldier had gone far away, and muttered, "Lili mama, unreasonable, foreign devil." Fortunately, he shook his head and stuck out his tongue, muttering to himself, "Hey, am I afraid of him?" I thought that the previous sentence was the sound of a weak nation, and the following sentence was the self-comforting words of the weak.

At that time, the general onlookers dispersed in a rush. Several joking friends laughed and shouted, "The country is going to perish, the country is going to perish."

My esteemed neighbor, that Wang tailor who usually loves to boast, was originally there too. Hearing the words of the two joking friends, he immediately struck his complacent and contemptuous pose, muttering,

"Perish, perish, will China perish? Do you know how many immortal masters and swordsmen on Mount Emei in Sichuan have not yet come down the mountain? Hey!"

He was about to continue speaking, but was dragged away by a child.

I was in a bad mood, standing there thinking, when I suddenly heard a friend in a very elegant Western suit complaining to his companion,

"Mr. Wang, how can you look into these things so closely? I just dragged you and you refused to leave. Alright, don't delay any longer, golf, golf!"

His companion smiled and followed him away. I followed them with my eyes and saw them strolling quickly and stepping into the small golf course across the street, which was full of red and green lights, with white-clad waiters and smiling foreign ticket girls with bare arms.

I exclaimed in shame, and said to myself, "This is the popular new game of the modern youth of 1931. No wonder he was so eager to get there!"

At that time, I walked away dejectedly. Before I reached the back, I saw a group of children under the eaves of the neighborhood house, surrounded by that Wang tailor, all smiling with their small mouths, listening to Wang tailor telling the story of "Journey to the West". They were really sitting straight and attentive, tasting the story better than they listened to the teacher in the small school, as if they were sitting on nails, much better than the uneasy look they had in class. There were even a few who, when their family called them to eat dinner, replied that they would wait a moment. When I saw this, I felt ashamed again, "Not bad, children's education!"

Youth Zone Guidelines 214

(1) Articles should be related to discussions on youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, and random thoughts. The style is not limited.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to those related to youth issues.
